Italian Postal Company's Fastest Liner to China 115

▲ Can reach Italy in 24 days

▲ Breaks all previous sailing records

▲ The fastest mail ship in the Far East

This year's competition among ocean liners is fierce. Major shipping companies are building ships with increased speed. Ordinary steamships with a speed of 13 or 14 nautical miles per hour are gradually being eliminated by the process of natural selection. In the Pacific this year, since the completion of the two giant liners, the Hoover and Coolidge from the United States, the speed of mail ships or cargo ships currently operating between the United States and China is around 19 to 20 nautical miles. On the European route, British and French postal services have also switched to newly built fast liners, trying their best to shorten the sailing time and save economic time. This is necessary to compete. Now, on the Sino-Italian route, there is an unprecedentedly fast mail ship sailing to Shanghai, breaking all nautical records and truly opening a new era in the Sino-Italian shipping industry. The details are as follows:

▲ Italian Postal Service Improves Passenger Liners The Italian Postal Company in Shanghai is boldly renovating its shipping business between China and Italy this year, dividing passenger and cargo ships into two categories. Four ships, including the Pilosna and Krakofu Quqi, are specially designated to carry passengers and are listed as official mail ships on the Sino-Italian route. Two other ships are specifically assigned to carry cargo. Passenger and cargo ships are scheduled to operate once a month, traveling between Shanghai and Qu Li in Italy. Only this Italian shipping company operates in Shanghai, so business is still good.

▲ Additional Special Fast New Ships Currently, after the British C-class new ships began operating on the European routes from Shanghai, the fastest time to reach London is 32 or 33 days, and other ships take 36 or 37 days. The four new passenger liners newly dispatched by the Italian Postal Company this year also take 33 or 34 days to reach Italy from Shanghai. Now, the company's newly built special fast giant liner, the Conte Roseo, has been completed. The ship has a load capacity of 17,240 tons and is dedicated to passengers, so it is equipped with first, second, and third class cabins, with excellent layout. The fuel is oil and the horsepower is very large. The speed per hour can be more than 20 nautical miles. It has been assigned to operate on the Sino-Italian route.

▲ Breaks Nautical Records According to the company, the new Conte Roseo is scheduled to depart from Italy in late January and will arrive in Shanghai in February. It is scheduled to depart from Shanghai on its first voyage to Italy on March 11. The ship's huge power and fast speed make it the unprecedented first ship on the Far East-Europe route. From Shanghai to Italy, via Hong Kong, Singapore, and the Red Sea, via Levant Brindisi Venice Priest, it only takes 24 days to reach. After the ship is put into operation, this Sino-European sea route can be shortened by one-third.

The Aftermath of the Burning of the Dade Ship 118

▲ Passengers' goods have been completely destroyed

▲ Nine corpses recovered from the Hupu River

▲ Bereaved families will make representations

After the burning of the Dade ship of the Shanghai Dada Company, the company sent the Dayu ship to the scene of the accident with the merchants who had goods on board and various insurance companies to investigate whether there were any remnants of the fire. The ship returned to Shanghai at 12 o'clock the night before last. According to the merchants, the 1,052 pieces of Western-style cotton candy, green licorice and tobacco that they had loaded were completely destroyed. Also, after the Chuheng ship arrived at the scene of the accident, it immediately cooperated with the Chuyuan ship to salvage corpses. Yesterday, the Hupu Post-Disaster Office sent a telegram saying that nine corpses had been recovered from the Hupu River. The company immediately replied by telegram, ordering them to take photos in Hupu, prepare coffins, and collect the corpses, and send the photos to Shanghai for identification. As for the Chuyuan and Chuheng ships, they are continuing to salvage corpses to avoid omissions.

The number of people burned to death and drowned in this accident is more than 120. Currently, there are people whose whereabouts are unknown and whose corpses cannot be found, such as Shen Zhuowu, Xu Yuanzhe, Xu Bingruo, Ge Xudong from Rugao, and Cheng Liu, etc. There are also those who are registered in other counties who are being investigated. Now, the families of the victims, in order to ensure the safety of travel for fellow villagers in Jiangbei, have decided to hold the company responsible for all legal responsibilities based on the company's failure to take precautions beforehand and its negligence in rescue afterward.

Shen Zhuowu's whereabouts are unknown. Upon hearing the news, the Rugao Chamber of Commerce and other groups immediately sent people to investigate along the Jiangbei ports and also sent people to Shanghai to comfort Shen's family and assist in the investigation. They also telegraphed the Civil Affairs Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, requesting them to order the water police in each district along the river to pay special attention to the search.

The Shanghai Municipal Government previously approved the Ministry of Finance's document based on the letter from the Flood Relief Committee, requesting exemption from the flood relief grain wharf donation. Continued Hearing of the Day and Night Bank Case 120

▲ Selling the Wannian Cemetery

▲ Retaining the Chu Jiu Hospital

The case of the bankruptcy and liquidation of the Shanghai Day and Night Bank and the Great World Amusement Savings Department was again summoned yesterday by the Civil Execution Court of the Second Special Court. Judge Wang Weizhen said to the lawyer representing the Huang family, "The Wannian Cemetery under the Huang family's property was mentioned during the last court hearing. I don't know if it can be auctioned. Have the directors discussed it?" Lawyer Tan Yigong replied, "The lawyers for the directors of the Wannian Cemetery have not yet known about it. Please grant an extension so that we can send a letter to urge the conclusion." Then, the lawyer representing the creditors, Yan Luqing, said, "According to our lawyer's speculation, the Wannian Cemetery may be of a business nature and can be sold. The court can clarify the situation by checking the accounts." Judge Wang also said that the court had recently received a letter from a certain public association requesting the purchase of the Huang Chu Jiu Hospital to establish a charitable hospital to help the poor, and the Social Affairs Bureau had also sent a letter expressing its agreement and requesting its retention. What is the opinion of the lawyers representing the creditors? Lawyer Tan Yigong, representing the Huang family, said, "This is a public welfare matter, and the Huang family does not object." Lawyer Yan Luqing, representing the creditors, said, "The Huang Chu Jiu Hospital is one of the Huang family's properties and should be listed for auction. The hospital is small and there are many charitable hospitals in Shanghai. The public association can buy property elsewhere and establish a hospital. Why should it take advantage of the poor creditors?" Lawyer Tan replied, "Even if the auction yields more one or two thousand yuan, each creditor will only get a few dozen copper coins more, which is not a big loss. Retaining this public welfare hospital benefits the people and is a great merit." Judge Wang instructed them to wait for a written reply for review and decision. According to the lawyer representing the creditors, Xu Yannian, "Since the bankruptcy and liquidation of the Gongfa Company, each creditor has only received 20%, and the rest of the money has not been settled. But I don't know what status the liquidator has in relation to Huang's property, whether it is issued by the liquidator or handled separately by the Huang family. Furthermore, the French Municipal Council has previously ruled that Huang's property is subject to provisional attachment. Please pay attention." Judge Wang instructed to check the files for review and decision, and then adjourned the court.

The Municipal Health Bureau Bans the Sale of Quinine Pills 121

Since the promulgation of the Regulations on the Management of Drug Dealers and the Regulations on the Management of Proprietary Medicines, the Municipal Health Bureau has been following them. In addition to issuing orders to all drug dealers to register in accordance with the regulations, it has also implemented drug inspections in order to prevent unsanitary and substandard drugs. It is now heard that Ke Fa Pharmacy is manufacturing and selling a type of quinine sulfate tablets (ie, quinine pills). The Municipal Health Bureau has verified that each tablet contains 0.006188 grams of cinchona sulfate and 0.07831 grams of cinchona hydrochloride, and does not contain quinine sulfate, which is inconsistent with the label on the bottle. This violates Article 22, Item 4 of the Regulations on the Management of Drug Dealers. The bureau has punished the pharmacy in accordance with the regulations and ordered it to send all the manufactured tablets to the bureau for incineration.

Lawyer's Application Form Format 124

The Shanghai Lawyers Association sent a notice to its members yesterday, stating that "Lawyers are entrusted by their clients to handle litigation cases. Except for using the name of an agent to make applications to the court, which must use a complaint, if the application is made to the court solely in the name of a lawyer (such as applying to review files, applying for an extension, applying for a sub-agent, or submitting a defense brief), it is not necessary to use a complaint. Only an application form is required, with a judicial stamp of one jiao. If it is a civil application for an extension or application for a sub-agent, a application fee of seven jiao and five fen must be paid. Because the number of new members is gradually increasing, we are concerned that the aforementioned methods are not well understood, and to prevent disorder, the association has prepared four types of application forms for the sake of uniformity. Each type is priced at three copper coins to cover costs. The forms have been submitted to the Second and Third Branches of the Jiangsu Higher Court and approved by the Ministry of Justice Administration under Instruction No. 17483. All four types of application forms have now been prepared. Therefore, we hereby notify you to check and collect them at your own expense."

The Zhihe Bank Case Proceeds to Reconciliation 125

▲ The Court Initially Grants Postponement for Trial

▲ To Allow Both Parties to Negotiate Everything

Following the collapse of Zhihe Yongji Bank, the First Special District Court appointed accountant Tang Zaizhang to audit the bank's accounts. Tang subsequently discovered that Shen Chengfu, son of the bank's manager Shen Yingxiang, owed a massive sum of over 3.2 million yuan and had fled. If this sum could not be recovered, creditors would face a minimum loss of over 1.2 million yuan. Therefore, a petition was filed with the First Special Court, requesting that the bank's shareholders Shen Qilang, Chen Yizhai, Xu Xieming, Qiu Dingfu, and Chen Rongchu bear the responsibility for the unpaid debts. A trial had already commenced, as previously reported. Shen Chengfu has now been apprehended by the police, and his debt should be dealt with. In recent days, prominent businessmen such as Yu Qiaqing and Wang Xiaolai have been mediating. Whether this will be effective remains to be seen. Yesterday morning was the scheduled date for the continuation of the case. The defendants' lawyers, Wu Jingxiong, Wang Fuchang, and Zhang Zhirang, requested a postponement to continue reconciliation efforts. Judge Li, considering the complexity of the case and the undesirability of prolonged delays, granted a brief postponement to allow both parties to negotiate everything. If reconciliation proceeds smoothly by the deadline, a further extension may be granted. If it proves difficult, the trial will commence to prevent undue delay under the guise of reconciliation. Both parties' lawyers agreed to this, and Judge Li granted the postponement.

Abandoned Infant Nearly Leads to Trouble 126

▲ Wen Zhongtian's Good Intentions

▲ Truth Revealed After Questioning

Around 6 PM the day before yesterday, a Chinese constable, number 3031, from the Xinzha Police Station found a man near the Racecourse on North Chengdu Road carrying the corpse of a girl about two years old. Finding his behavior suspicious, the constable took him to the police station for temporary detention. The child's body was transported to the autopsy center on Fielun Road. Yesterday, the suspect was transferred to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Judge Wu Tingqi questioned the man, who identified himself as Tian Zhongwen, from Suzhou, age 46,

Page 16

a small vendor, residing at No. 12, Yangguan Lane, west of the Racecourse. Yesterday afternoon around 3 PM, he said, "I saw a girl of about two years old abandoned on the ground in the lane, still breathing. I took pity on her. As the orphanage was nearby, I picked her up and took her to the Dagu Road orphanage. However, the orphanage clerk said that someone had brought the child an hour earlier, but they refused her due to her serious illness. Since I was doing a good deed, they suggested taking her to a charitable organization in Zhabei, which would likely accept her. They gave me 300 copper coins to hire a rickshaw. However, I didn't know the way, so when the rickshaw reached Zhabei, I couldn't find a charitable organization, and the driver didn't want to continue. I had to turn back to the concession, and near the Racecourse, I asked the constable where to take the child. The constable, seeing that the child was dead, took me to the police station. I have an elderly mother, wife, three sons, and a daughter at home," and he began to weep uncontrollably. Subsequently, police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that Tian Zhongwen was a key witness in the case and should be temporarily detained until after the autopsy. Judge Wu instructed that Tian be released after the autopsy. Prosecutor Guo then arrived by car to examine the body, confirming that the girl had died from illness. As no relatives could be found, the Pushan Mountain Villa was ordered to bury her. Tian Zhongwen was released.

Three Suspects in the Zhu Yangshan Family Murder Retract Their Confessions 127

▲ Denying Robbery and Murder

At 1 AM on September 19, thieves broke into the home of Zhu Yangshan, a native of Qingpu, at 196 East Xihua Road, stealing valuables worth several thousand yuan and killing Zhu's relative Gu Cao, and a maidservant Zhou Lu. Huishan Police arrested Ma A'er, a rickshaw driver from Tongzhou, based on information from Cai Zhitian. He was handed over to the First Special District Court, tried, and sentenced to death, pending approval from higher authorities. On the afternoon of the 2nd of this month, Detective Xie Shuiquan of Huishan Police and Detective Lu Gengsheng of Diswei Road Police arrested Zhang Xianjun (nicknamed "Little Yellow Hair"), from Tongzhou, and suspects Yang Douchu and Qu Hanming on Fair Road. They also went to Zhang Xianjun's home at No. 8 Tangshan Road and arrested his brother Zhang Xianming, and friends Ji Haikun and Li Helong, a total of six people. Zhang Xianjun, while being led by detectives to identify the scene of the crime at the victim's home, suddenly collapsed, having been injured in the head by handcuffs. He was sent to the police hospital for treatment. The next morning, the police handed over Zhang Xianming and the other five to the First High Court for detention. This was reported in this newspaper. Subsequently, the police determined that Yang, Qu, and Li were not involved and requested their release. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao Xiebin specially convened the Fifth Criminal Court to investigate. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that Zhang Xianjun had recovered, and Ma A'er had also submitted a petition from the Western Prison. During the ongoing investigation, it was discovered that Zhang Xianjun and Ji Haikun had committed eight robberies between last month at No. 186 Huishan Road, No. 93 Huade Road, No. 56 on the same road, No. 214, No. 528 Yulin Road, No. 38, No. 2 Huasheng Road, and No. 8, stealing clothing and silver worth several hundred yuan. The victims were all present, and some of the stolen goods were recovered from various pawnshops. The prosecution requested that the robbery and murder case be heard first. Zhang Xianjun confessed to the police that Ma A'er had initiated the plan, inviting him along with "Long Black Charcoal" and two men from Qingkou. Ji Haikun also went. Long Black Charcoal and the Qingkou men climbed over the wall by stepping on each other's shoulders. Long Black Charcoal and the Qingkou men held the knives. After the fact, they were given 15 yuan. Because Long Black Charcoal knew the murdered maidservant Zhou Lu, he killed her. Long Black Charcoal was also known as "Turtle." At the time, Zhou Lu called for help. Zhang Xianming firmly denied involvement, claiming he had been in his hometown. Ji Haikun admitted that Ma A'er had initiated the plan and Zhang Xianjun had invited him. Long Black Charcoal stood on Ma A'er's body, Ma A'er stood on Zhang Xianjun's body, Zhang Xianjun stood on Ji's shoulders, and they climbed over the wall. Ma A'er and Long Black Charcoal committed the murder. Afterwards, Long Black Charcoal pawned the stolen clothing. After being apprehended, the detectives led them to the victim's home to reenact the events, which matched Ma A'er's previous confession. The confessions of the three defendants were presented. Subsequently, Zhu Fu, the wife of Zhu Yangshan, stated that her husband operated a pawnshop at 196 East Xihua Road. She and her husband had gone to Wuxi for medical treatment when the incident occurred. The murdered were her relative Gu Cao and the maidservant Zhou Lu, who were guarding the house. The 430 yuan in silver was spent in May. The stolen clothing consisted of fine furs, a total of ten boxes, nine of which were opened. Only one purple fur coat was recovered. When newly made, they were worth 6,000-7,000 yuan. She did not recognize any of the defendants and her husband had no enemies. She believed the servants had leaked information about the family's trip to other places. Judge Xiao ordered the three defendants to be questioned separately. When Zhang Xianjun was questioned, he completely retracted his confession to the police, claiming that he had returned to his hometown with his wife, brother Xianming, and two friends on July 10 to celebrate the festival and worship their ancestors, returning to Shanghai on August 18. He denied going to the victim's home, killing the two women, and stealing the clothing. He claimed that his confession to the police was false. The court declared, "There is no need for you to quibble. Ma A'er has already confessed in detail." He was ordered to present Zhang Xianming's confession, who stated that he, his brother Xianjun, and his sister-in-law returned to their hometown together on July 10. His brother only stayed in the hometown for half a month, then returned to Shanghai with his sister-in-law first. He arrived in Shanghai on August 28 and knew nothing about the murder and theft. Ji Haikun also denied all of his confession to the police. Ma A'er also claimed not to recognize the three defendants. Even he, himself, admitted that his death sentence was unjust. Judge Xiao further questioned the three defendants in detail, pointing out contradictions. All of them denied going to rob and murder. The court then heard the robbery case, and ordered them back to detention to await further questioning.

French Police Strictly Prohibit Gambling 128

▲ Yang Jinsheng Fined 800 Yuan

Detective Lu Jinchen, Deputy Detective Wang Rusong, Mao Jinsheng, Bao Detective Jiang Changwen, and others from the French Concession's Great Bell Police Station discovered that Yang Jinsheng, a Suzhou native, was privately operating a gambling den at No. 8 Jiruli, Jixiang Street, gathering people to gamble on Pai Gow and skimming profits, in violation of the prohibition. The previous night, they raided the place, confiscating gambling tools, dice, and 17,256 yuan in gambling money, and arrested 30 gamblers along with the owner, Yang Jinsheng. The gamblers were fined 10 yuan each for participating in gambling. The gambling tools and funds were confiscated.

Bank Tea Server Sentenced for Stealing Large Sums 129

▲ Sentenced to One Year and Eight Months Imprisonment

Song Yexi, a tea server from Anhui working at the French Avenue branch of the China Industrial Bank, took advantage of the absence of the teller on October 9, when Kong Bingjun was substituting, to secretly obtain a key, open the safe, and steal 3,800 yuan in banknotes. He used the money for gambling. The case remained unsolved. On the night of November 22, he stole a blank check from the branch manager Shen Yangnong, filled it out for 105 yuan, and tried to cash it at the head office on Beijing Road. He was discovered, and the returned check notified the branch. The police were notified, and they located Song hiding at his home in Wandang Lane, West Gate. Detective Mao Shengsheng and Bao Detective Jiang Changwen went to arrest him, finding a secretly made key and a Jin Cheng Bank passbook, along with suspects Jian Gurong and Song's father, Song Hailin. All were arrested and transferred to the Second Special District Criminal Court for investigation. After two hearings, the defendant Song Yexi confessed to the theft. Jian and Song's father denied collusion. The court declared the debate closed, awaiting a scheduled verdict. Yesterday, the date for the verdict arrived. At 10 AM, Judge Xiong presided over the First Criminal Court, ordering the defendant to be brought to court and declaring the verdict. Song Yexi was sentenced to one year and eight months imprisonment for theft. The number of days he was detained before the verdict would be counted as two days of imprisonment for one day of detention. The key was confiscated. Jian Shunrong and Song Hailin were acquitted.

Yesterday at around 11 AM, a large bus No. 4033 of the Shanghai-Taicang Long Distance Bus Company in Zhabei set out to Jiading to pick up passengers. The three children were very close to Zhao, Chen, and Zhao, and seemed reluctant to part with them. Bank Association Discusses Abolition of Floor Price for Public Bonds 137

▲ Both Exchanges Request Abolition of Floor Price

▲ Ministry of Finance Orders Bank Association to Discuss

According to the East China News Agency, the Ministry of Finance recently received requests from the Shanghai Chinese Business Securities Exchange and the Commodities Exchange regarding the previous restriction on the minimum price of all public bonds, which the Ministry of Finance had imposed to maintain the price of public bonds, prohibiting prices from exceeding the standard of November 24. Since the implementation of this measure, the credit of public bonds has been maintained, but the responsibility of the exchange to balance market conditions has been constrained, and the bond market has become stagnant. Therefore, they recently requested the Ministry of Finance to abolish the order restricting prices. The Ministry of Finance reviewed the results and believed that the abolition of restrictions was greatly related to the rise and fall of public bonds. To handle this matter carefully, they ordered the Bank Association to discuss and decide and submit all opinions to the Ministry of Finance for reference. The Bank Association held a meeting at 2 PM yesterday to discuss this matter. The discussion concluded that the Ministry of Finance has the authority to maintain public bonds. The previous restriction on price drops was a fundamental way to maintain bond credit. If the Ministry of Finance believes that this abolition is feasible, the banking industry should comply and not object. The results of the meeting were sent to the Ministry of Finance last night to report everything.

The Restoration of the Commercial Press Union 142

▲ Workers' Delegation Has Implemented the Takeover of the Publishing Industry Branch Office

Because the workers of the Commercial Press opposed the Publishing Industry Union, they automatically convened a general assembly on the 10th of this month and elected a 27-member delegation responsible for maintaining it for several days. It is also reported that yesterday morning, Wang and Yang and others were unwilling to accept this and hired many thugs to try to regain the union office. The workers' maintenance team prepared by the delegation was also on high alert, so the situation was extremely bad, but fortunately, no accident occurred. Municipal Government Approves Temporary Suspension of Harbor Quarantine Fees for Boat Owners 147

Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Government responded to a petition from Xing Zhigang, a representative of boat owners from Pudong Xihang, stating that the harbor quarantine office violated principles and imposed exorbitant fees on civilian ships, requesting that the relevant departments be instructed to effectively stop this practice to avoid disrupting municipal administration. The reply stated: "The petition and attachments have been received. Currently, an order has been received from the Ministry of Health of the Interior to temporarily suspend the procedure and submit alternative methods for review. This has been stopped. Therefore, in addition to the instruction, this reply is hereby issued for notification."

Random Words of Dogs and Horses 172

— Qingqu

Inukai Tsuyoshi is an old member of the Japanese Civil Party and an old friend of our country's Sun Yat-sen whom he had been deeply associated with thirty years ago. This time, Mr. Inukai, as a supporter of the Seiyukai, did not hesitate to use his seventy-year-old head to re-enter the political arena to show his tough and aggressive plan and extend his wrist to our Northeast, and will soon fully achieve the ambitions inherited from the Tanaka era. Inukai Tsuyoshi's cabinet formation poses a very pressing threat to our country's future.

Yesterday, I chatted with my friend Mr. Qin Musan. Mr. Qin also sighed when he heard about this. Then he slammed the table and said, "Why are you so worried?" When asked why, he said, "Even if Japan has dogs, it doesn't know that our country has horses. Although dogs are larger than dogs, they can't guard the house. Forming a cabinet with dogs is just a puppy. How can it be better than a horse that can gallop away from the dust, carry soldiers to victory on the battlefield, and better defend our borders?" I then knew that using "horse" to counter "dog" was a coincidence. Because "Yang Yi" has "Xiufang" two words in it, it is enough to be it. Now General Ma Zhanshan is fighting Japan with a single division in a desolate area, which is admired by the whole country. Everyone knows his name, but doesn't know that his name is "Xiufang", which is inevitable. I realized that using "Xiufang" to counter "Yang Yi" is truly a solid and accurate match. Mr. Qin really has a different understanding. Fang has this expression, or some say that "Xiufang" two words are too soft, not as rigid as "Yang Yi". I said no, no, not so. Our country has always advocated peace, and gentleness is enough to overcome rigidity, and rigidity is ultimately disturbed by gentleness and frustrated to annihilation. There are many in the world who do not know it. So the discussion was settled. Asked Yu Zhi to fulfill this talk.

Record of the Recently Lost Dede Wheel 173

— Cheng Zhizheng

In March of this year, the Daji wheel of the Dada Company caught fire midway, causing a tragic death of many lives. The reporter once wrote to record it. After a short period of time, the company's Dede wheel was again heard to have been burned. The huge number of casualties and the heavy losses were more than before. It is truly an unprecedented catastrophe at sea.

It is found that Dada Company was founded by the late sage Zhang Jizhi of Nantong. Those who travel outside the Yangtze River were initially Daji, Dashun, Dede, and Dahe wheels. Later, Daji and Dashun were sold or re-routed due to the small size of the wheels. The company added Daqing and Daji wheels to undertake its scarcity. The Daji was destroyed in the spring. Recently, it has been repaired and launched and renamed Dayu. In fact, the company currently has four wheels, namely Dede, Dahe, Daqing, and Dayu.

The four wheels travel between Shanghai and Yangzhou, and their lives are prosperous. Dayu and Daqing are new ships, with larger tonnage and better equipment. Dahe has the best machinery and travels quickly. Dede is weak and weak. People in Tongyang call it "old woman". They are reluctant to take it unless they have to. From Tong to Shanghai, other wheels can arrive at noon. Dede does not handle it until 3 or 4 pm. In recent years, the machine parts have been slightly changed, and there has been slight progress compared to before. In the eyes of Tongyang people

There is a long way to go. I sincerely hope that the directors of the company can be determined to reform and live up to the hard work of the late sages.

Enlistment 175

—A member of the Youth Aid Ma Garden Team

(3) Leaving Zhenru

On the morning of the ninth, after we thanked the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of Jida University, the entire team headed towards Nanxiang. In less than an hour or two, the destination was seen. There were welcoming civic representatives at the station. We were very ashamed to be welcomed and encouraged by them at Guyi Garden. We stayed at the Central Elementary School at night.

Originally, we didn't have to walk. Because the central government has understood us and has given us first-class vehicles for the group to ride in. But we only accept the government's kindness and thank the government, but the whole group decided not to ride in the prepared vehicles. Because this can show the perseverance of our youth. It can also hone our courage. To prepare for going to Heilongjiang.

In the afternoon, civic representatives from Kunshan and Suzhou came to inquire about the itinerary and dates. It is said to be convenient for welcoming, etc. But we think to ourselves. It is the duty of the people to sacrifice for the country. Now it is disturbing the people of all walks of life. The center can't help but feel bad.

On the tenth, a member withdrew. He originally did not want to withdraw. Because the people in his family said, "If you don't go back, the whole family will die in Nanxiang." But all of our members joined voluntarily. When joining, the review team must carefully consider it. The military knowledge, endurance, and whether there are family burdens, etc., of the members must be asked clearly before they are considered qualified. There is no form of inciting or forcing young people to join. Therefore. We also have to persuade him to withdraw when this member refuses to go back.

An Elegant Gathering Amidst the Winds and Cranes 176

— Jing Mengdie

In Lanling, there was already a Chrysanthemum Society. Every year, when early winter arrives, as the chrysanthemums by the fence are not yet withered and the plum blossoms on the mountain ridge are about to bloom, the host of the society, Mr. Xia Yihe, would always send invitations to guests to drink and compose poetry at Yi Garden. This year, due to the national crisis, his mood was desolate. He sent a letter in advance to consult with me. I said, "The purpose of an elegant gathering is to meet friends, not only to appreciate flowers but also to express sorrow, not to seek pleasure." Yihe then entrusted me to write a small announcement in place of invitations, saying, "Smoke of war fills the land, the wind is bleak in the north. The cries of wild geese echo, autumn ends in the south of the Yangtze River. Facing the shattered rivers and mountains, we shed tears at Xinting in vain. Moved by the desolate scenery, we cannot forget the flowers of the old garden. Thus, a mere scholar has held a thorn for ten years, harboring thoughts of joining the army, but finding no way to offer his services. Those who live in luxury are not worth consulting; we might as well submit a memorial to the northern palace. A writing brush is truly useless; it can only write rhymes by the eastern fence. Perhaps drifting on the lakes and seas, we encounter the winds and cranes in a foreign land. Separated by mountains and passes, we miss the water shields of our homeland. Perhaps bound by mossy rocks, we deeply cherish the clouds and trees. Stealing a day of leisure, we console each other about the three lives. Therefore, we agree on an auspicious time to re-invite old friends. Holding crabs, we face the chrysanthemums; arm in arm, we enter the forest. Wine can dispel sorrow, temporarily easing our solitary indignation. Flowers can understand words, sharing our hidden feelings. We entrust ourselves to the sorrowful songs of Du Fu, mourning like Changsha. May Gao has a pen; for whom does he dash off urgent letters? Xu Mian is affectionate; let him calmly judge the winds and moon. Let Tao Yuanming seek intoxication, and the Chu guest eat the fallen petals. This is also a helpless time, an unavoidable matter. Alas! Bind Du and Yin high in the pavilion, just to avoid becoming worms in the river. Tread the fragrant garden of peach and plum. Come quickly! Appreciate the falling snow before the flowers." When the appointed time arrived, the guests arrived. Old friends such as Zhuang Jichen, Zheng Zhongxiu, Fang Huqing, and Zhang Baixi, a total of ten people, sat around a table. What the guests discussed was the situation of the national crisis; what they heard was news of the national crisis; what they saw was writing about the national crisis. It was no less than opening a Gandhi-style round table conference. The host smiled and said, "Tonight, we can only talk about the winds and moon." A young guest said, "But what if the nest is overturned and no egg is left intact?" I said, "If the Wang Yifu types of that era were not in court but in the wilderness, then their empty talk would not have led the country astray. Moreover, we have no weapons in our hands; our pens cannot be turned into guns. Even if we want to save the country, our strength is insufficient. Compared to those officials and military men who hold a non-resistance doctrine, and those important figures in the party-state who destroy unity and invite foreign insults, causing concerns about partition and joint control, then we truly should not talk about national affairs." The guests were silent. Looking around at the chrysanthemums, although the flowers bloomed not near the battlefield, they all carried a sorrowful and sickly appearance, unlike their spirit in previous years. Perhaps they were also affected by the times. I could not help but think of the saying that even trees are like this.

Mr. Gao Junshan Returns from Europe and America to Discuss the National Crisis (II) 177

— Jiping

American students have a weak sense of political awareness. Therefore, they do not pay much attention to the figures on the political stage, nor do they understand them very well. Some college students do not even know the structure of their government. In our country, not to mention college students, even some middle school students know it very well. Everyone can name who the key figures in the central government are and who the chairman of a certain province is. In America, ordinary students probably know more about movie stars and sports heroes than they know about figures on the political stage. In America, during elections, such as elections for president, governor, or mayor, each state, city, and town has polling places. However, many, many people do not participate in voting. It is not necessary to discuss general civil cases. Even among the intellectual class, there are many people who give up their rights. In short, they do not feel a strong interest in politics.

Recently, in our country, due to the national crisis, the people of the whole country feel the pain of national demise is imminent. They have unanimously made suggestions and petitions to the government. Innumerable young students are running around appealing and demonstrating. The public is furious, wanting to give a resounding blow to the numb and insensitive authorities. I believe that this kind of patriotic movement is respectable in its ambition, but its situation is extremely pitiable. People who are in their study years should not be made to go to study quietly, and instead, go and engage in political activities. Enduring hunger and cold is not even the worst part. Sometimes they have to suffer the schemes of villains and the oppression of the authorities. What a disservice this is to them. Some people say, "Students should not be involved in politics." I think this is a very natural inclination in a country with clear and bright politics. Just look at the American college students' interest in politics, and you will know. But in a collapsing and fragmented China, there are constant and intense stimuli. How can students maintain a calm attitude towards politics? The saying "Saving the country does not conflict with reading" is theoretically correct. But in this moment of crisis, when survival is at stake, how can you make them read in peace? The so-called "saving the country through education," "saving the country through industry," and other terms are all applicable to peaceful times. But the biggest key at the moment lies in politics. The government authorities can bring prosperity with a single word, and destroy the country with a single word. If politics is not on the right track, then education, industry, and everything else are hopeless. Some people also say that during the Franco-Prussian War, even with the sound of cannons faintly heard outside Paris, the students in the city could still calmly attend classes. Of course, they had great generals who defended the country and protected the people, fighting the enemy on the front lines, without worries about the rear. Looking back at our country, what is it like? When enemy troops approach the border, they abandon their weapons and flee. Within a few days, they lose the territory of three provinces. How can this be compared to France? Therefore, the fact that American students are not interested in politics is their blessing, not their weakness. Compared to them, the students in our country are much more unfortunate.

Rotary Club Book Review

Sharing the Same Hatred with You (16) 178

— Gu Mingdao

Chapter Four: Righteousness Obliterates Kinship

The next morning, Hua Naiqiang finished breakfast and was sitting in the guest room, feeling depressed and studying a map. Suddenly, Zhongshu gracefully entered, her face showing worry. Naiqiang invited her to sit down and said to her, "Looking at the map, there is a high mountain southwest of T city. It leans against the mountain and borders the river, making it a good place to defend. It can serve as a shield for T city. For the sake of preparedness, why doesn't your father quickly send a brigade of troops to garrison there, to block the enemy's path of attack?" Zhongshu stamped her leather shoes and said, "Brother Naiqiang, why keep talking such nonsense? Let me be honest with you. My father has already surrendered to the Sun Army." When Hua Naiqiang heard this, he jumped up and said, "How… how could he willingly surrender to the bandits?" Zhongshu said, "Last night, my father spent the entire evening discussing military affairs in a secret room. I went over there to spy and saw several Sun Country people inside, acting suspiciously and not knowing what they were discussing. I was very suspicious. For a while, I couldn't find my father. I ran to my father's room this morning to ask, and then I learned the truth. Alas…" Zhongshu paused as she said this. Hua Naiqiang said, "What is the truth?" Zhongshu said, "Originally, my father was tempted and coerced by the people of the Sun Country, and he changed his mind. He is willing to be their lackey and is about to send troops to attack H Province. I heard that a large batch of weapons and ammunition from the Sun Country will be transported here today to supply my father's army. Tomorrow, they will attack H Province. Brother Naiqiang, what should be done about this? I am unfortunate to be the daughter of a traitor. I think it's better to leave this place. I really can't bear to see this sad situation." Hua Naiqiang clenched his fists and slammed them on the table, saying, "Traitor! I shouldn't be scolding your father in front of a lady. He really is blinded by greed, not wanting to have his name remembered forever like Zhang Qiaoyang, but willing to imitate Wu Sangui and leave a stinking name for ten thousand years. Old and muddled to the extreme. China actually has this kind of soldier. My blood is boiling! Traitors should be killed by everyone." After Hua Naiqiang finished speaking, his face turned green with anger. Zhongshu covered her face and wept. After a long while, she said, "I have no face to live in the world. I'll just die. Brother Naiqiang, please take care of yourself for the sake of the country. It's best to leave this place as soon as possible." Naiqiang rubbed his hands, just thinking deeply. Zhongshu's words were as if he hadn't heard them. After a moment, Hua Naiqiang shook his hand at Zhongshu and said, "Lady, don't cry. I've come up with a plan. I don't know if you agree." Zhongshu stopped crying and wiped away her tears with a handkerchief. She asked attentively, "What good plan is it?" But Naiqiang hesitated and said, "It's hard to say." Zhongshu said, "Anything can be said. There's no one around here. Tell me quickly!" Hua Naiqiang walked to her side and whispered many words into her ear. Then, with both hands, he stood back by the table, waiting for her to decide.

Cotton Yarn: The Cotton Yarn Market's Situation Weakens Daily 184

The cotton yarn market is generally sluggish, and the situation is weakening. This is primarily due to the instability of national affairs and the extreme tightness of finances. Most people in the market are bearish. However, demand from Sichuan and Changsha merchants is relatively strong, while other merchants are mostly inactive. Nonetheless, manufacturers are still buying when prices fall.

Forward Wheat Market: Improves 190

▲ Wheat Factories Continue to Take Delivery This Month

Yesterday, the forward wheat market was generally stable after opening in the morning. Sentiment was relatively stable because foreign wheat prices fell by 0.06 or 0.07 yuan. However, trading was very quiet, with both buyers and sellers taking a wait-and-see approach. By the afternoon session, market sentiment had improved. Since factories continued to take delivery this month, approximately 20 to 30 truckloads were taken. Sentiment suddenly improved, and because there were fewer sellers and eager buyers for distant months, prices were driven higher. As a result, the price for this month rose by 0.04 yuan compared to the previous day, the price for January rose by 0.05 yuan, the prices for January, February, and March rose by 0.04 yuan, the price for April rose by 0.02 yuan, and the price for May rose by 0.01 yuan.

Piece Goods: Eastern Goods Secretly Resurge 192

Eastern goods and piece goods had disappeared from the market since the invasion of Manchuria by Japan, due to patriotic citizens' economic boycotts. It has been almost three months, and inspections are not as strict as before, and goods have dropped drastically in price. Certain individuals are taking advantage of this situation, especially by relabeling goods, which is especially prevalent for colorful velvet. Labels are cut off and replaced with domestic labels, and the goods can be sold unhindered. Fine cloth, twill, serge, etc. have also been discovered, which has hurt the sales of genuine goods. Although it is approaching the New Year holiday, and despite internal and external pressures, the infiltration of Eastern goods is significant. White velvet was especially sluggish yesterday. Double Fish and Jiqing at 16 pounds have entered the lower price range. Dasheng Electric at 10.035 taels was very slow moving. Only Jincheng at 9 pounds was quite strong, requiring 6.95 taels. Spot goods were scarce. A large batch of Dasheng to Peacock fine cloth was offered at 7.5 taels, and there was significant inbound buying in this area. Yuanfang's bidding has resumed after stopping the second round, and prices are slightly better. Yuanrong and bleached cloth remained unchanged. Yu Chou silk was slightly more active. Fairly priced Tianci Huangjin Qiaofacai was 14 taels, Sanyou Tu was 13.75 taels. Coarse cloth was in a complete slump. 9 pounds were at 4.78 taels, 11 pounds fell to 5 taels, and 13 pounds were around 6 taels. Only Wuhe at 16 pounds remained at 8.2 taels. Coarse twill was also weak.

Book Review

Japanese Imperialism's Economic Aggression Against China – and Collection 195

By Hou Houpei and Wu Juenong

Published by Liming Publishing House

China's writing circles are inherently impoverished; there are deficiencies in writing in all areas. But comparatively speaking, works on Japanese imperialism, especially after the September 18th Incident, are more plentiful than in other areas. From major works of two or three hundred thousand characters to small booklets of several thousand characters, given the impoverished state of the publishing industry, it cannot be considered completely silent. And among these numerous works studying the Japanese problem, we cannot help but highlight this book, "Japanese Imperialism's Economic Aggression Against China," co-authored by Hou Houpei and Wu Juenong. The reasons can be divided into:

First, as the authors said in the preface, "Japan has been plotting aggression against China for a long time. This occupation of Manchuria and Jehol is a full expression of Japanese imperialism's aggression in China. Although the incident occurred in a violent form, whether for immediate or long-term reasons, it is fundamentally backed by economics. Japan's economic power in China is more advantageous than that of other countries, and its methods of economic aggression are also more active. The success of economic aggression against China is the success of Japanese imperialism's continental policy." Using economic aggression to explain the entirety of Japanese aggression against China truly grasps the core of the issue. Understanding the content of Japanese economic aggression against China allows one to know the entirety of Japan's ambition and methods for invading China. Current books on the market about Japanese imperialism either only consider one aspect of the problem or only the surface. This is one difference between this book and others.

Second, Japanese aggression against China is a complete problem, not a partial one. In other words, Japanese aggression against China has a consistent policy and is definitely not a local or one-sided issue. For example, Tanaka's active policy of aggression against Manchuria and Mongolia states, "Using the rights in Manchuria and Mongolia as a command tower, we will seize all of China's resources. Using China's resources, we will conquer India, the South Seas Islands, Asia Minor, and Europe. Our Yamato race's desire to display its military prowess on the Asian continent depends on holding the rights in Manchuria and Mongolia, which is the first key. Moreover, ultimate victory relies on food supplies, the prosperity of industry relies on raw materials, and the strengthening of national power truly relies on China's vast territory." Thus, local records or narratives cannot explain the consistent policy of Japanese imperialism's aggression. Most of the books on Japanese imperialism on the market are biased toward one aspect, especially the three eastern provinces. Little do they know that Japanese imperialism's aggression against China is progressing on multiple fronts, and each front is mutually supportive. Therefore, the Manchurian Incident is just one part of Japan's total aggression against China, or rather the most obvious part. But if one wants to understand Japan's entire policy of aggression, one must further understand the economic power of its headquarters in China. Moreover, one can say that without understanding Japan's total economic power in China, one cannot have a correct understanding of the Manchurian Incident. This book's perspective is national, not limited to any one part. Of course, Japan's economic power is most significant in the three eastern provinces, but there are many economic matters that the three eastern provinces do not possess. This book's sources are balanced, which is another point of difference from all other books in this area.

Third, materials are the lifeblood of a book. To put it bluntly, the quality of a book depends entirely on its materials. Currently, the materials used in books on the Japanese problem are mostly outdated and copied repeatedly, without questioning the source of the materials, leading to errors being passed on.

It is truly rare to have "original materials," that is, "direct materials." This book, however, "uses all actual materials for objective narration... The collection of materials is primarily based on direct sourcing, either through personal direct investigation or by collecting business reports, meeting minutes, and rosters that the Japanese do not normally circulate outside, and compiling them. Therefore, the various statistics in the book are quite detailed. Other materials taken from various Chinese and Western books and newspapers are also carefully referenced and corrected before being transcribed." Leaving aside other things, the book contains many secret reports obtained by Japanese ronin, such as the so-called Records of the Manchuria and Mongolia Rights Support Conference revealed by the Yishi Daily. For example, statistics on Japanese enterprises in Shanghai and statistics on exporters have not only been unknown in the past, but even with the intention to investigate, it would be difficult to get results. This is what makes this book inaccessible to other books in this area.

These three points are the main differences between this book and other books in this area, and they are also what make this book surpass other books.

The authors believe that "the policy of Japanese imperialism's economic aggression against China is nothing more than two things: investment in China and seizing the market. The structure of this book is based on these two policies. The first chapter explains the origin of its economic policy towards China and its methods of aggression. The second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, and seventh chapters are about investment and the market, respectively narrating the steps of its aggression and its recent situation. The eighth chapter is about the financial institutions that assist investment and market aggression, exploring the inevitability of Japanese economic aggression against China. All economic aggression matters such as railways, shipping, agriculture, forestry, mining, industry, trade, and finance are included." The table of contents for the entire book is thus divided into: Chapter 1: Japan's Economic Aggression Policy Towards China; Chapter 2: Japan's Railway Aggression Against China; Chapter 3: Japan's Navigation Rights Aggression Against China; Chapter 4: Japan's Agricultural Aggression Against China; Chapter 5: Japan's Mining Rights Aggression Against China; Chapter 6: Japan's Industrial Aggression Against China; Chapter 7: Japan's Trade Aggression Against China; and Chapter 8: Japan's Financial Aggression Against China. The entire book is four hundred pages and

Amounts to two hundred thousand words. It must be considered a comprehensive overview of research on Japanese imperialism and aggression against China.

Researching Japanese imperialism's economic aggression against China

Easily flows into a defect, which is that it is either empty theory without empirical evidence or a chronological account without theoretical explanation of the facts. As mentioned above, this book's actual materials are not only rich and complete but also mostly direct and new. So, is this book just a presentation of facts without correct theoretical elucidation? Definitely not. The book's theoretical consistency and depth have equal value to the materials it has collected. In many places, it is insightful and expresses what others have not. For example, in the first chapter, the authors correctly point out that the origin of Japanese economic aggression against China is due to: first, overpopulation and food panic; second, lack of raw materials and difficult livelihoods; and third, opening up markets and developing trade. Its means of aggression have always been nothing more than three kinds:

1. Coercion and Enticement Policy: Regarding this point, the authors say, for example, "In the Sino-Japanese War, our country failed and signed the Treaty of Shimonoseki. When Yuan Shikai proclaimed himself emperor, Japan coerced our country into signing the Twenty-One Demands. The Jinan Incident and the Mongolian Incident in 1928 are all manifestations of the coercion policy, that is, the so-called active policy of Tanaka, or the policy of forcibly seizing rights and cultivating trade." As for the Japanese government's coercion and enticement policy toward local military figures, the examples are too numerous to mention.

2. Seizing Profitable Rights Policy: For example, "The previous railway competition, loan competition, the development of the South Manchuria Railway Company's business over the years, and the construction of the textile industry in the Yangtze River basin all demonstrate Japan's investment policy. The most significant was the conclusion of treaties with Japan during the period when Duan Qirui presided over the cabinet in 1917 and 1918, including the arms loan, wireless telegraph loan, forest development loan, Jilin loan, and reconstruction loan. At this time, Japan lent huge sums of money to China on the one hand and used them as collateral to plunder its profitable rights and property, thereby developing Japan's economic power in China."

3. Undermining Peace Policy: This section is even clearer and more profound: "Divide and conquer has been Japan's traditional policy toward China in recent years. As early as 1916, the assistance to the Zongshe Party's uprising and the assistance to Duan Qirui's training of the war participation army in 1918 were all clear evidence of promoting internal strife in our country. Guo Songling's revolt and Japan's dispatch of troops to southern Manchuria were to maintain the old pro-Japanese forces in Manchuria. During the Northern Expedition, troops were repeatedly sent to Shandong in order to maintain the remaining warlords of Zhili and Shandong. Zhang Zuolin was bombed in Huanggutun after the failure of the Feng clique, which was an attempt to support new forces in Manchuria and Mongolia. Since then, the Northeast has changed into an anti-Japanese force. Thus, the Japanese became vigilant and uneasy, and finally took the recent action of occupying Manchuria and Jehol..."

Among Japan's economic aggression against China, the main points are investment and market. Japan's investment in China can be divided into two major categories. One is state capital, that is, in the name of the Japanese state.

Page 22

Or by directly lending money from Japanese state banks to the Chinese government, or investing in a certain enterprise, such as the 2.15 million yen Jichang Railway loan that China borrowed from Japan in 1909, and the 10 million yen postal loan in 1911, are examples of this. The second is Japanese financial capitalists, that is, those called zaibatsu by the Japanese, who invest in various Chinese enterprises, aiming to obtain various profitable rights. This capital invades our country's agricultural, forestry, commercial, mining, transportation, factory, and other enterprises. Wherever there is profit to be made, it almost penetrates without any barriers. This investment is centered on the three eastern provinces and rooted in the Yangtze River area.

In addition to investment, the next is market aggression. The importance of Japan's market aggression against China can be seen in the statement made by Secretary-General Tomita Kojiro at the 59th annual meeting of the Japanese Minseito, "No market is closer to Japan and more closely related than the Oriental market. However, Japan does not seem to have given due importance to the important Oriental market. Whether it is to China or to the South Seas, the majority of its exports and imports belong to European and American countries. Looking at the import trade on the Chinese side, Japan can only account for 30 percent of it, and the remaining 70 percent are not ours. Abandoning such a large adjacent market is not the way to develop Japan's national economy. Therefore, we must adopt a guiding and friendly policy to deal with the so-called Oriental markets, such as China." This shows its ambition and eagerness for market aggression against China.

Although the various sectors of Japan's economic aggression are interconnected and whole, each has its own means or strategies. This book has extremely detailed descriptions and disclosures about this matter. Amid the active aggression of Japanese imperialism, this book is indeed an excellent reference for understanding the methods and nature of Japanese aggression. In summary, the important features of the entire book can be divided into four types:

1. The actual statistics of Japan's economic aggression against China are accurate and complete, with everything that should be there.

2. Most of the materials taken are recent and direct materials, which are difficult to collect and are extremely valuable.

3. The entire book takes China as a whole as the subject of discussion, not only focusing on a part of the three eastern provinces. Wherever Japanese economic power reaches, such as the Yangtze River basin, everything is described in detail.

4. Equal emphasis is placed on theory and facts, using actual materials to prove the theory, and using in-depth theory to reveal the facts, without any dryness or empty talk.

History of Japanese Imperialism's Invasion of China by Ai Xuan 196

(4) The author divides Japan's invasion of China into four periods: (1) The Tentative Period (1867-1893). During this period, Japan forced China to sign several unequal treaties, namely the Sino-Japanese Treaty of 1874 and the Tianjin Treaty of 1885. (2) The Incipient Period (1894-1904). During this period, Japanese imperialists greatly expanded their aggression. Our country ceded Taiwan and Ryukyu, lost Korea, and paid an indemnity of 350 million taels. The conclusion of the Boxer Protocol and the outcome of the Russo-Japanese War led to the situation where "Japanese power already dominated Manchuria, and Manchuria was in peril." (3) The Active Period (1905-1914). Japan's operations in Manchuria achieved great success due to the signing of various unequal treaties. (4) The Unbridled Period (1914-Present). Japan brazenly revealed its ferocious face, acting recklessly with the Twenty-One Demands, the Changchun Incident, the Fuzhou Incident... and the recent Jinan Massacre, as well as the current violent occupation of the Eastern Provinces, are the highest points in this history of aggression.

Above, the author provides a very simple explanation of the various factors in this history of aggression. Without understanding the driving forces of history, how can one understand historical facts? The author's efforts in this work are to help us understand and interpret history. This is a part that readers should not ignore.

The second part describes the facts of the invasion of China over the past sixty years, divided into four periods according to chronology, with detailed and concise narration. It is a very good historical resource. At the end of the book, a chapter has been added recently, namely the case of Japan's forcible occupation of the Three Northeastern Provinces, divided into the following sections: (1) The eve of the tragic incident; (2) The course of the tragic incident; (3) The process of our country's concessions and negotiations. At the end, the author said with great indignation: "I believe that since Japan is deliberately planning to permanently occupy Manchuria and Mongolia, no matter whether this case is handled by the League of Nations or through direct negotiations, there will be no good results. It can be asserted that national subjugation is near. Instead of sitting and waiting for death, why don't our 400 million compatriots bravely rise up and fight to the death with Japan? It is better to be a ghost of war than a slave of a conquered nation. My compatriots, strive for it, strive for it!"

"This attitude is probably the attitude of every reader. The third part is "A General Statistical Analysis of the Achievements of the Invasion of China in the Past Sixty Years." This is a horizontal record. From various statistical figures, every reader will be shocked to realize the "struggle for interests" of the imperialists. The whole article is divided into five parts: territory, military, political, economic, and cultural. Each part provides readers with many factual proofs and large numbers to prove how China is being trampled under the iron heel of Japan.

In the conclusion, I completely agree with the author's opinion. He said, "China can either choose not to survive, or if it wants to maintain its survival, it must rise up and overthrow the Japanese imperialists who are hindering China's survival.

"From the perspective of the survival of the Chinese nation, China is an oppressed nation, and Japan is the most ferocious imperialist oppressing China. Standing on the viewpoint of national equality and the requirements of national survival, we must resist Japan's oppression. We demand the freedom and independence of the Chinese nation, to liberate our nation from the layers of oppression from Japan.

"From the perspective of the mission of the Chinese National Revolution, imperialism is the only target of the National Revolution. If imperialism is not overthrown, the National Revolution will never be successful. The National Revolution and imperialism cannot coexist. In order to complete the National Revolution, we must also overthrow Japanese imperialism.

Only resisting Japan can save the country, and resisting Japan will surely save the country. The author explained it very clearly. I sincerely recommend this book to every reader, and I hope that every reader can learn historical lessons from this book, awaken, and be inspired.

Each issue is sold for one dime, and all newspaper vendors, theaters, and bookstores have it for sale. Special discounts are available for subscribers. The annual subscription of 52 issues, including postage, costs only four yuan, and a copy of "Human Beauty" worth one yuan and two dimes will be given as a gift. Subscriptions can be made directly to the Dongfang Yinshuguan on Haining Road, or contact the Xiaoxiao Bookstore on Sichuan Road.

Four famous film critics in Shanghai have been hired as editors, and the content is specially designed for the benefit of readers. With an impartial perspective, they will provide practical guidance and faithful introductions to the films to be shown in various theaters in the week, and explain which film is suitable for the psychology of which type of audience. A special column will reproduce the descriptions of various new films, revealing them without omission, so that people will know the detailed plot of each film before watching it. Movie fans in this city should read it first. Box No. 2009, and the society will send the full year on schedule.

Medical News 198

▲ The China Mental Hospital declares that it has been established for more than ten years and has a well-established reputation. Recently, the number of people seeking treatment has been increasing daily. Therefore, the No. 1 Hospital on the Xinji Bin Road is no longer sufficient, and a No. 2 Hospital has been set up to admit inpatients. Mr. Jia Chengxiu of Fu Xiangji on the Dazimingzhong [Big Bell] in the French Concession suffered from pain in his right leg, making it impossible for him to move an inch and restless day and night. After being treated by this hospital, he recovered and was discharged from the hospital in less than ten days. Recently, Mr. Jia intends to publish a thank-you notice to praise the hospital.
